          --monorail-metadata-toggled-bg: var(--monorail-metadata-closed-bg);
        }
        mr-issue-page[codeFont] {
          --mr-toggled-font-family: Monospace;
        }
        .container-issue {
          width: 100%;
          flex-direction: column;
          align-items: stretch;
          justify-content: flex-start;
          z-index: 200;
        }

          flex-grow: 1;

        }

          width: 100%;

          height: calc(100vh - var(--monorail-header-height));
        }
        mr-launch-overview {

Email display settings

<h2>Email display settings</h2>



        

There is a 

setting

<a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a>

 to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.

<p>There is a <a href="/hosting/settings">setting</a> to control how
        your email address appears on comments and issues that you post.</p>



        

Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.

<p>Project members will always see your full email address.  By
        default, other users who visit the site will see an
        abbreviated version of your email address.</p>



        

If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there
        are other ways to 

get
        involved

<a href="http://www.chromium.org/getting-involved">get
        involved</a>

 in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item
        on the "Help" menu.

<p>If you do not wish your email address to be shared, there

        involved</a> in the community.  To report a problem when using
        the Chrome browser, you may use the "Report an issue..."  item

This site hosts public issues in public projects

<h2>This site hosts public issues in public projects</h2>



        

Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.

<p>Unlike our internal issue tracker, this site makes most
        issues public, unless the issue is labeled with a Restrict-View-*
        label, such as Restrict-View-Google.</p>



        

Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.

<p>Components are not used for permissions.  And, regardless of
        restriction labels, the issue reporter, owner,
        and Cc'd users may always view the issue.</p>

 of his. It is also a resource deadlock which defines that the issue has freezes the application and/or crashes. In this case, it is causing the Chrome Beta Webview engine to crash. comment#12



<a class="undefined" target="_blank" href="#c12"><!---->comment#12<!----></a>





, I haven't understood it completely but tried to reproduce it and getting that error in adb. But it looks like that this bug is like a too many draw calls in a too short period of time. I don't know about the actual boundaries completely. As per that, the bug was fixed using `glFinish()` and `glFlush()` will force the application to wait until the rendering queue has been emptied. Apparently, the GPU (or the GPU driver) will panic when the queue has too many entries. The GPU driver is running in kernel space and in order to communicate with it, the application (usually abstracted by a graphics framework, like e.g. OpenGL.ES) has to send according ioctl messages.



<span class="line"><!---->, I haven't understood it completely but tried to reproduce it and getting that error in adb. But it looks like that this bug is like a too many draw calls in a too short period of time. I don't know about the actual boundaries completely. As per that, the bug was fixed using `glFinish()` and `glFlush()` will force the application to wait until the rendering queue has been emptied. Apparently, the GPU (or the GPU driver) will panic when the queue has too many entries. The GPU driver is running in kernel space and in order to communicate with it, the application (usually abstracted by a graphics framework, like e.g. OpenGL.ES) has to send according ioctl messages.<!----></span>

<span class="line"><!---->libGLESv2_adreno.so one is crash in the gpu driver. Also libhwui is the android java view compositor, not webview.<!----></span>

output_surface_provider_webview.cc one is webview intentionally crashing (SIGTRAP, not SIGSEGV) on gpu context loss



<span class="line"><!---->output_surface_provider_webview.cc one is webview intentionally crashing (SIGTRAP, not SIGSEGV) on gpu context loss<!----></span>



<br>

There are lot of GPU related crashes on android, but we (the chromium team) do not control, have access to, or can influence what GPU driver other device manufactures ship to their users.



<span class="line"><!---->There are lot of GPU related crashes on android, but we (the chromium team) do not control, have access to, or can influence what GPU driver other device manufactures ship to their users.<!----></span>



<br>



<br>





If you can reproduce something consistently on a google-produced device, then we can look more. We have overall crash monitoring and we do investigate issues that affect a lot of devices. But if you are just reporting a one off thing on a non-google device, then there isn't much we can do.

<input id="targetProjectInput" aria-owns="chops-autocomplete-1" aria-autocomplete="both" aria-expanded="false" aria-haspopup="listbox" aria-activedescendant="">


              




      


        /*
         * Really specific class names are necessary because ShadowDOM
         * is disabled for this component.
         */
        .chops-autocomplete-container {
          position: relative;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container table {
          padding: 0;
          font-size: var(--chops-main-font-size);
          color: var(--chops-link-color);
          position: absolute;
          background: var(--chops-white);
          border: var(--chops-accessible-border);
          z-index: 999;
          box-shadow: 2px 3px 8px 0px hsla(0, 0%, 0%, 0.3);
          border-spacing: 0;
          border-collapse: collapse;
          /* In the case when the autocomplete extends the
           * height of the viewport, we want to make sure
           * there's spacing. */
          margin-bottom: 1em;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tbody {
          display: block;
          min-width: 100px;
          max-height: 500px;
          overflow: auto;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr {
          cursor: pointer;
          transition: background 0.2s ease-in-out;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container tr[data-selected] {
          background: var(--chops-active-choice-bg);
          text-decoration: underline;
        }
        .chops-autocomplete-container td {
          padding: 0.25em 8px;
          white-space: nowrap;
        }
        .screenreader-hidden {
          clip: rect(1px, 1px, 1px, 1px);
          height: 1px;
          overflow: hidden;
          position: absolute;
          white-space: nowrap;
          width: 1px;
        }
